<Author>Kurosaki
<Content>Overly-pretentious, indifferent service. My partner and I chose the Sir Francis Drake because of its reputation as one of the oldest and finest hotels in SF. Unfortunately, while it certainly had quite a history, our stay was forgettable at best, and disillusioning for the most part. To be sure, the location was good. (But there are a ton of other hotels near Union Square.) Rooms were clean, although tiny. Despite our request at the time of booking for a higher floor room, we were put on the 4th floor, where the noise from the cable cars plying Powell Street were in full surround sound. The amenities were also not as the hotel website promised. The complimentary high-speed internet access was not at all stable, and kept falling off. Cable TV was also restricted to CNN and Disney. The corridor smelt funny for a couple of days - like cat food. The staff were also indifferent. Our luggage took 40 minutes to be delivered. Housekeeping continually failed to replenish amenities like shampoo and notepads. Front desk was also incompetent at dealing with customers. At one point, there was a row of customers queueing up to complain about something or other about their room and reservation. We were finally forced to find another hotel to stay for the second of our two-week stay in SF.

<Author>codash
<Content>Old but great Make no mistake - this is an OLD Hotel and in some areas needs some fairly drastic renovation. With that comment in mind I have to say that I could not fault this hotel in any other respect.I last stayed at the Sir Francis Drake some 40 years ago and since my memory was a little vague, I contacted David Watkins (he was responding to comments on TripAdvisor at the time) for assistance. His response was quick and most helpful. The arrangements he made for me were marvellous and I am sorry he was not there for me to thank him in person. I had a Queen room in the tower block with a view over Union Square. There was some noise from the nightclub 2 floors above but it was tolerable and did not go too late. The bathroom was, as many have commented, small but it was adequate.The hotel staff are excellent in the full Kimpton manner. I had stayed a few weeks before at the Pacific Pallisades in Vancouver and my expectations were high. They were met and exceeded. I should particularly mention the doorman, Tom, in his (fake) Beefeater costume. He was extremely helpful both to guests and in fact to any passer-by who stopped to seek directions and advice.I apologise for getting a window stuck in the open position. which necessitated a call to engineering. Their response was prompt and friendly. However it did illustrate the age of the builing.I would have no problems staying there again.

<Author>Scooper80
<Content>A new favorite in SF My mom and I met in SF for a long weekend and stayed at the Drake. We absolutely loved this hotel! Prior to booking our room, I signed up with Kimpton's rewards program, which I totally recommend doing! A few days before our trip, I received an email from Kimpton about a one day sale. I was able to book an executive double room for the same price as a standard double, plus we were given 50% off of all bottles of wine while we were there. Check in was a snap; our room was ready, the front desk staff was pleasant and poliet and willing to answer any questions. Kimpton rewards members are given a card for a free glass of wine at the lobby bar, which I quickly put to good use! Our room was great; nice linens on a comfy bed, turn down service with yummy chocolates, enough room for the two of us plus all of our purchases (we did a LOT of shopping). The rooms are typical SF-size. Don't expect a massive room; these are older buildings! We had an issue with the bathroom light shorting out, requiring us to call maintence. The problem was fixed very quickly, and both maintence and our housekeeper stopped by again to ensure that the problem had been resolved and we were happy. We visted Scalas for dinner one night---soooo yummy, I highly recommend it! We also had drinks at the Starlight Lounge, which gives an incredible view of SF. We also went to Sunday's a Drag (a drag show brunch in the Starlight Lounge). The show was fun, but the buffet was pretty awful. We both said it was the first time we had been to a buffet brunch and left NOT feeling stuffed or really full. Tip: they say the show is sold out as of Saturday evening, but if you show up on Sunday morning, before the show, they usually have a few cancellations and can squeeze you in. We did this and were given a table (in the back, however). Check out was easy-I used to tv menu to do so. They were more than willing to hold our bags while we shopped and had lunch before our flights home. In general, the staff was beyond courteous and helpful. We were really impressed with their attitudes and willingness to answer questions. I'd definately come back to the Drake. It is a fantastic hotel for the money, and we actually enjoyed it a great deal more than the St Francis (our previous favorite), which is great since the Drake is significantly less expensive.  
<Date>Nov 18, 2008

<Author>tamasutra65
<Content>Room to Small My husband and I stayed at the Drake for a long weekend in November. It is in a great location, just off Union Square and right in front of the Powell Street cablecar stop.The staff is very friendly and check in was quick.If you like hotels that aren't cookiecutter and don't mind small rooms you may like this hotel. I have stayed at other Kimpton hotels and quite liked them. I did get a very good rate by booking through their Web site. For this visit I booked a deluxe queen room but was upgraded to a queen room in the tower. The room was quite small with a queen bed and a desk with desk chair. There was no sofa or other chair to sit on and was not room for anything more. The bathroom had a tub that needed to be repainted, a small sink and a toilet. Very little room for toiletries.We had to live out of our suitcase because there was little room for clothing. The wallpaper in the bathroom was gouged in places. The door to the bathroom was difficult to close and stuck when it was finally closed.Overall we had a very nice stay in San Francisco, but I wouldn't book this hotel again because of the small rooms.

<Author>prycehudson
<Content>It's a little piece of history... The rooms are on the small side but in comparison to a NYC, London or Paris hotel...it is comparable. What I enjoyed most was the hospitality. <Author>YorkTravelGirl
<Content>Good stay, except for the bed My husband and I stayed at the Sir Francis Drake for two nights as part of a driving trip down the coast of California. Though all problems that we had with this hotel were taken care of, I would not stay here again.Our check-in was slow because there were many people in line at the same time. This wasn't anyone's fault, but it was a bit annoying. When we did finally get our room, we noticed that it was a smoking room. We had requested a non-smoking room because smoke really bothers my allergies. When we double-checked with the front desk, they said this was a non-smoking room; however, someone had clearly been smoking in it. They graciously changed our room; however, this one had its own problems.The second room, on its surface, looked ok. It was small but relatively nice -- or at least that's how it looked until we pulled back the comforter on the bed. When we settled in for the evening, we noticed that there was a blood stain and several other white stains on the sheets. We found this absolutely repulsive, but because I was so sick that night, we just threw a towel over it and slept on it anyway. The sheets were changed the next day, and the desk staff was very accommodating, but I would still not stay there again.

<Author>Archipelagic
<Content>Exceptional hospitality wraps perfect package at Sir Francis Drake After seeing the mixed reviews the Sir Francis Drake had drawn, I decided to experience it myself and see if it met my high standards. It far exceeded even my high expectations. When I have the good fortune to return, I will hope stay at this property again. The exceptional quality of the hospitality wrapped up a perfect package for a five day stay. The service was obliging, efficient, and friendly. Staff sometimes added the personal touch of addressing me by name. From managers to the staff at the registration desk, from the bellstaff to the incredibly resilient crew of hardy and handsome gentlemen who form the ranks of the Beefeater costume-clad doormen, I was impressed with how everyone on the team exerted themselves to provide a top-notch experience for hotel guests. Rooms- (I had more than one, and loved both) were exquisite, beautifully appointed, great views, quiet, very comfortable beds, and during the warm days the air conditioning worked well. Remember that at the time this hotel was built, these WERE big rooms: houses and beds were all smaller then. I found the room generously proportioned.Lobby and lobby bar - The lobby is spectacular, lovingly restored, and the design of the bar in the lobby defines the space while paying homage to the existing interior design and decor, rather than intruding upon it. There is a vibrant atmosphere in this central space, and the service was wonderful. Restaurant : I visited the adjacent restaurant -- a separate business -- on several occasions for dinner and/or drinks. The service was superb (although the restaurant is popular so if you want a table you may wish to consider reservations at dinner) and the food was absolutely excellent every time.Night Club - There is also a night club on the top floor that has a great view and is very popular. I ventured up one evening and although I had just missed that evening's live music, the joint was packed until closing.In my view the address is the perfect one for a San Francisco hotel. Great atmosphere. Just out the front door many opportunities beckon for people who like to people watch, shop, and eat. Location is fabulous for walkers, cable car devotees and public transit, and taxi. Just a short slide of less than a block down Powell St. puts you at Union Square.I visited a friend at another Kimpton property not far away, the Sorrento, another lovingly restored historic property, and it was also lovely, the friend's room excellent, and the friend's report on the place was positive.

<Author>TracyJG
<Content>Great hotel - superb staff We stayed at the Sir Francis Drake for 5 nights in July. We booked the hotel due to its central location just a few steps away from Union Square and all the great shops and we weren't disappointed. Chinatown is also within walking distance and the cable car stops right outside the hotel for getting to Fisherman's Wharf. From the moment we checked in the staff were courteous and helpful. Unfortunately during our trip I had a bike accident and had to attend the hospital to get stitches in my leg. Hilary (the concierge) went out of her way to help by phoning the doctor and the hospital as well as Blazing Saddles Bike Hire to sort things out for us. The bar staff (especially Aaron) were also very friendly always saying hello and enquiring how I was doing. We had breakfast most mornings in Sears (directly across from the hotel) which was really good. We had dinner in EO Trading, Neptunes Palace at Fishermans Wharf and the Cheesecake Factory in Macys. We also ate in the hotel restaurant Scala's. The food and atmosphere was great - very handy when you don't feel like walking too far.All in all I would thoroughly recommend the Sir Francis Drake to anyone staying in San Francisco. The actual hotel is nice but it is the staff that makes it stand out from the rest!

<Author>Purn
<Content>Comfortable but Anonymous Stay at Sir Francis Drake The best feature of this hotel is its central location and the close proximity to Union Square. Sir Francis Drake has an entrance and lobby which is reminiscent of the architecture that a London West End theatre would have. The charming cable cars- which are symbolic of San Francisco- stop outside the hotel before climbing its way up Nob Hill. The bedroom was decorated to a unique taste, but even by European standards was small. It was clean and comfortable. The TV was positioned parallel to the bed and so you had to turn your head by 90 degrees if you wanted to view it in bed. The air-conditioning worked efficiently but its vent was positioned directly above the bed, making it uncomfortable to lie beneath.America is renowned all over the world for having good customer service and the staff at the Sir Francis Drake was no exception. <Author>bkimberly
<Content>Great Stay at Sir Francis! We spent five days at the Sir Francis Drake and loved it. The architecture and decorating in the lobby are really fantastic. We got a corner room on the 20th floor with a spectacular view of the city. The room was very clean and the linens were top quality. The staff was courteous and accommodating. Ryan, one of the Valets, was so attentive and professional---he really took care of us. I know many reviewers complain that the hotel is old. This is true and you have to expect certain things when you choose to stay at a historical location--the rooms will be smaller, the water pressure may not be great, and you will be more likely to hear noise in the hallways from your room. This comes with the territory. Appreciate historic hotels for what they are and what they can offer---beautiful and unique original fixtures, architecture, service, and the nostalgic feeling you get when you walk in the door.

<Author>karmaghost
<Content>Nice hotel, only a few issues We stayed at the Sir Francis Drake for our honeymoon and overall we really enjoyed our stay. The location is hard to beat, just seconds from union square and right in the heart of activity in San Fran. If you've never been to SF, the hotel is right on Powell Street, which is where the famous cable car trolleys can be found.The concierge downstairs was very helpful in suggesting restaurants, directing us to the proper bus stops, and setting up our wine tour of Sonoma and Nappa Valley. After checking in and then coming back from dinner during our fist evening, we found a bottle of wine and some biscotti along with a note from the hotel congratulating us on our marriage and welcoming us to the hotel (although they spelled our last name wrong, not a huge deal).The room itself was fairly spacious (we were in the executive king on the 8th floor) and had some interesting details. The bathroom was very nice, with black tile, a bath/shower and even a separate shower stall which I thought was an interesting touch. The complimentary soap and shampoo was AVEDA, which my wife tells me is a nice, high-end brand. My only issue with the bathrooms was that there wasn't a lot of counter space and we ended up keeping a lot of our toiletries and other items on the floor next to the sink.There were a few issues, besides the lack of counter space in the bathroom, that we experienced while at the Sir Francis Drake. The first thing we noticed was that our windows, on the outside, were absolutely filthy. It looked as though years and years of buildup had accumulated on the two large windows of our room and, I'd say, quite severely obstructed our views of the city. For this reason, we kept our light-cloth blinds drawn at all times, which was a shame as the view from our room was something we were looking forward to when we arrived. Another issue presented itself on our last night in the hotel; the air conditioning unit (which is located in the ceiling with intake and blower vents) started to leak onto our ironing board, on some of our clothes, and soaked the carpet that one of our larger suitcases was resting on. We noticed this in the middle of the night when a strangely loud *pat, pat* of dripping water could be heard in the middle of the night. Because it was our last night at about 1am, we didn't call the front desk because we decided a repair situation or a move from our current room was not what we needed the night before our morning flight back home. When I approached the front desk to check out, I made a point to bring up the inconvenience with the A/C. The clerk seemed helpful, but informed me that there was nothing he could do to compensate me for the problem since we had prepaid and booked our stay at Hotels.com and had no extra charges to the room. All in all we had a nice stay in the Sir Francis Drake, but it was unfortunate that our final memories of the hotel will be slightly tainted with the issues with the A/C that couldn't be resolved.

<Author>brianpre
<Content>A Very Disappointing Four Days I was booked with three colleagues for four nights at the Sir Francis Drake. Each of us were to have had our own room. However, when we arrived, we learned that the hotel was overbooked and they doubled two of us up. My room (1530) had a steam pipe that sounded like a drummer in a rock band all night long. The apologetic engineering staff told me there was nothing they could do because the pipe could not be accessed easily. It was impossible to sleep that night. In the morning, I asked for another room. They moved me, but nobody ever apologized for placing me in an uninhabitable room to begin with.The hotel is old and the rooms are comfortable, but small. The windows didn't appear to have been washed in years. The configuration of my bathroom (room 1519) was bizarre to the point that using the toilet was a physical challenge (and I'm not big, 5' 10).One night the airconditioning went out in two of our rooms, and the electricity failed in another. All in all, it was not up to standards for was should have been a first-class hotel. The final problem was that on the day of checkout, two of the three of us had unauthorized charges on our bill. Again, we were not met with apologies from the staff, but suspicion (Sir, are you certain you didn't use the lobby bar?).I could have stayed at the Westin, which is just down the street and next time I certainly will.

<Author>7johnny
<Content>Excellent Stay at the Sir Francis Drake Hotel Let me start by saying that I'm the cynical type, so if I write something nice about a stay, the place just might be worth a look . . . If you are seeking a grand hotel, a smaller version of New York's Plaza Hotel, then you've come to the right place. With a location in the Union Square district, it is just about as central as you could want to be. They've spent a lot of effort overhauling this building and it shows; just the right combination of old marble and new interior design. Transportation: outside is the cable car, though you should walk a couple of blocks down the hill to catch it, because it's filled to the brim with tourists by the time it passes the hotel. Go a couple of blocks further down the hill and catch the underground. Secret: To get to fisherman's wharf/alcatraz, if you get fed up waiting for the cable car, hit the underground; take it out to the embarcadero/ferry building and then take a trolley along the waterfront to the wharf. A lot less crowded . . . On the return, retrace your steps but at the Ferry Building, walk toward the subway and take the OTHER (Powell/Hyde?) cable car back home, since its not crowded. Get a map from the concierge and you'll get the picture.Shopping: One door down is Saks Fifth Ave. Turn the corner and you are in the shopping district if that is your thing. It's much denser shopping than New York; you get every brand on top of each other in a few blocks.Amenities: Rooms are recently upgraded and it shows. Comfortable and quiet. The staff are exceedingly helpful. A concierge and doorman who actually know the town well and have a great attitude.The lobby is seriously cool. With a two-story ceiling, nice arrangement of sofas, chairs, and a bar, its not too big, just about right. Tourist Attractions: You can easily walk to Chinatown and the City Lights bookstore. For points beyond, the hills can be a challenge; buses are plentiful. Get a 3 day pass down the block across from Macy's. You can buy half price theatre tickets there too. Eating: Streetlevel is leased to Starbucks and an upscale restaurant. We ventured a few blocks out and there are loads of places to eat. If we saw a mob of tourists, we just moved on. There are very few bad choices as far as eating in that area. Oh yes, and if you want to get snacks for the room, go across the street to Walgreens, which seems to be open all night. Photos: I google streetviewed this place and it looks small from the outside, but isn't. They've wisely leased their frontage space to the starbucks and scala's restuarant. Actually, the hotel covers half the block. In closing, a really great place to hang your hat while you're staying in San Fran.  
<Date>Aug 25, 2008

<Author>tc_kmc
<Content>Regrettable Experience I booked 3 rooms for 4 nights through Expedia.com in August 2008, and given our experience an overall rating of two is generous. The bright spots of our stay were Rachel at the front desk who was extremely pleasant and helpful and the nice Bellman who assisted us at the end of our stay (we had 7 in our party). Aside from these two points our stay was regrettable. I will admit that I have some blame as to the confusion with our room situation because I booked through Expedia (which I will not do again). Through Expedia they had a contract with the hotel for King rooms only (which was not clarified until after booking). As I finalized our plans I realized that I had 3 king rooms reserved and I needed three doubles, again I admit this was an error on my part; however, the treatment I received from the Kimpton reservations desk, the in-house reservations agent and the General Manager (who I emailed and didn鈥檛 respond) was very rude and unhelpful. It was as if because I booked through Expedia I did not deserve the same service as any other guest. Needless to say I was not able to change any of our rooms to doubles but again Rachel was very helpful and arranged roll-a-way beds for two of the rooms. As one of the other reviews mentioned when we arrived there was not a Bellman insight and we were not offered one at anytime during our check-in process. Two of the rooms were freezing cold as it was in the 50鈥檚 during our stay. In one of the rooms there was an inch gap where the two windows should meet and we had to put towels in the space to keep the heat in. In the other room the window in the bathroom did not go all the way up and there was a large opening. In order to keep the heat in the room we had to keep the door to the bathroom closed making it most unpleasant taking a shower in the morning. Requests for additional blankets, towels (since we used them in the windows) and an iron took two to three calls each. We were unable to get the Concierge at all and when someone at the front desk answered they gave us the wrong number three times and then charged me for three calls from our room!! In regards to the Beefeaters that everyone thinks are such a great attraction the one in the evening was VERY rude and the one in the morning was completely unwilling to be of any service, he acted put out if you asked a question. The Sir Francis Drake, although beautiful on the exterior, has marginal rooms at best and a staff that leaves much to be desired. I will not stay here again nor will I recommend it to anyone traveling to San Francisco.

<Author>erinwyher
<Content>The Drake - Central location in SF, Rooms nice and updated Our recent stay at the Sir Francis Drake was just perfect. The hotel was full of international tourists and wedding guests which was probably because our stay was in mid-August and also because the hotel is central to the touristy area. My husband and I stayed for three nights over a weekend.When I checked into the hotel on Thursday, I told the clerk at the front desk that I absolutely had to have a quiet room. I made it pretty clear that I wouldn't be happy in a room with any noise since I'm a light sleeper and have had trouble at a different hotel. The request was successful :). Our room had only light street noise. I personally do not care about a view and I didn't have one because of my quiet room request.One thing to note about this hotel is the lacking coffee service. There's coffee in the lobby only in the very early morning hours. This worked out for my husband and me because we stayed on Eastern time during our stay, waking up at 5am and going to bed at around 7pm or 8pm. The coffee was usually taken away by 7am or so. My husband conjectured that they might have had a deal with Starbucks which was located off of the lobby. Another thing to note was that the curtains in the room blocked the light from the street incredibly well. It made staying on Eastern time that much easier.The bed was incredible. The room was a bit tight but not by San Francisco standards. The tv stations were lacking; we probably should have brought some DVD's to watch during our down time.

<Author>ATLesquire
<Content>Very pleasant experience My 21 y.o. son and I had decided to visit San Francisco and then tour Sonoma Valley. I was looking for a convenient hotel and one that would not break my budget. (My son, of course, has no budget!). I looked at the reviews of several hotels and liked the comments about the Sir Francis Drake. What particularly impressed me was the response of the manager, David Watkins, to the complaints posted by several people who had stayed. (I considered some complaints legitimate; others seemed to be by people who had different expectations of a downtown-boutique hotel.) I contacted David directly, and after exchanging email, I made my reservations.The desk clerk who checked us in, Ryan, could not have been more friendly. He was extremely courteous and professional. When I asked if the WiFi service was free, he said that there was a charge but if I joined the Kimpton Rewards program, there would be no fee. Naturally, I joined. He also upgraded us to a room on the 20th floor. We had arrived a little early, and Ryan said that our room was not yet available but that he would put a rush order on it. My only disappointment came when I asked if David was on duty. Ryan said that David had transferred to another Kimpton hotel and was no longer at SFD. I had really hoped to express my appreciation to David in person. As I waited for the bellman to store our bags, after about five minutes, Ryan came over and said that our room was ready. We were able to go to our room immediately without having to store our bags.We had a nice-sized room with two queen beds. The beds were extremely comfortable, and the air conditioning was excellent. From some of the other reviews, I had expected practically opaque windows. That was not the case. The windows were slightly dirty but cleaner than I had expected. Additionally, we were able to open one of the windows and, thus, were able to get some great pictures without the glass interfering. The vanity in the bathroom was very small, and there was no place for our shavings kits (however, I had expected this from the reviews). We were able to manage this situation, however, with little problem. The location was great. We walked around the neighborhood and then took the cable cars when we ventured to Fisherman's Wharf. I recommend Sears for breakfast (a great restaurant just across the street). I asked Ryan for dinner recommendations at Fisherman's Wharf, and he recommended Scoma's. My son and I dined there that night, and it was excellent.I highly recommend SFD. I note that the new manager continues David's practice of monitoring this website and trying to solve probems that guests have encountered. That speaks highly of the Kimpton group of hotels.

<Author>KBSilverSpring
<Content>Won't be going back to the Sir Francis Drake I left the Sir Francis Drake unhappy, and would not go back. I will start with the basics; room size was fine, with a good walk in closet and nice toiletries in the bath. But there was only one chair, a rolling computer desk chair. The bath towels were coarse, the only towel rods were inside the bath tub. A tiny shelf over the toilet was the only dry place to sit anything. The vanity, a large boxy useless thing, had no shelves or door. The bathroom door wouldn't close. The room had AC, but it was as loud as my window AC unit at home. As it cycled on and off it would wake me up. All of these points my husband and I would've overlooked, if we had not had a bad night during our stay. The SFD was hosting a wedding reception our first night. Some of the guests appeared to be staying on our floor . After 1 AM we were awoken by drunken people coming off the elevator cursing at the top of their lungs. My husband got up, opened the door a bit and told the people to keep their voices down. A young man, in a tux, cursed at my husband and kicked our door in. My husband slammed the door shut and called the front desk to report the incident. Later we spotted someone who looked like security walking the floor. It took a long time to get to sleep after that excitement. The next morning we realized the chain lock had been broken and the door was scratched. So we reported it to a young lady at the front desk on our way out to breakfast. The front desk had not heard about the incident from the night staff, so we repeated the report. The clerk apologized and offered to move us. We declined that offer and asked that they fix the lock. The clerk also walked around the corner and told a 'manager' what had happened, I heard her. By the time we got back from breakfast the lock was repaired. That was the last we heard from hotel management while we were there. The incident wasn't the hotel's fault, but the control of guests at hotel receptions is their responsibility. I expected a Manager would contact us at some point during our stay to check on us but no more mention was made, even when we checked out. It left a bad taste in my mouth. I canceled the one night we had booked for a week later. When I got home a full week after our stay at the SFD, there was a survey from Kimpton waiting on my computer. I completed it, in full detail. Two days later a Manager from the Sir Francis Drake called me. He had never heard about the incident, not after our 2 reports to staff and the repaired door lock. He apologized and explained that even though the wedding party had spent around $20,000 at the hotel, that didn't give them the right to disturb other guests. I agree with him on that. He also said he would tell the hotel catering group. But its a shame that I had to fill out a post occupancy survey to get a Manager's attention. We are not ones to make a stink, but being nice quiet guests doesn't get you anywhere. We were just a couple of tourists staying for a couple of nights. Obviously we ranked far below a pricey wedding reception. The SFD didn't go that extra distance for us. There are other places to stay in San Francisco where we would be treated with more concern, we won't bother with the SFD again.

<Author>style_uncompromised
<Content>Functional stay for non-representing conference visitors San Francisco is similar to many European cities, but still not. The Sir Francis Drake hotel represents some of those typical differences by being an unusually large and anonymous hotel. The hotel is however perfectly functional, as expected and desired for this particular trip. A surprisingly small room compared to other US hotels I have stayed at, priced only slightly lower vs competition. The helpful and service-minded staff was highly appreciated. The hotel is centrally - and safely - located, with excellent shuttle bus connections to the Moscone congress centre and to the tourist parts of the city. The location guarantees nearby quality shopping and many reasonable restaurants for all your meals. Strikingly similar to the neighbouring hotel Westin St Francis. My recommendation is to confidently book either of them for a short, practical congress stay without required representation. The Ritz Carlton or Fairmont qualify better for the last part, however bear in mind then the cost will also be very different.

<Author>T. Advisor King
<Content>Getting older, not better I stayed in the SF Drake on business for three days. I understand that the hotel is 鈥渁 classic鈥?and tried to give it the benefit of the doubt, but ultimately, it turned out to be a hotel I wouldn't recommend.  In the heart of downtown San Francisco, the SF Drake is only a couple blocks from Union Square and Chinatown, and maybe a 15 minute cable-car ride from Fisherman鈥檚 Wharf. The cable-car stop is right outside the hotel鈥檚 front door, which is very convenient. The hotel is 鈥渙ld鈥?in more of a classic sense than a run-down sense. But once you get past the impressive d茅cor of the lobby, it really doesn鈥檛 offer anything exceptional in the way of comfort, amenities, or even ambiance.  Our room was an 鈥渋nside鈥?room on the sixth floor, which means we had a view of the back of another building and, as a result, were subjected to the constant drone of the ventilation/air-conditioning system. This wasn鈥檛 a big problem, but it was like having a bathroom fan going constantly. It was one of the smallest hotel rooms I鈥檇 ever stayed in. There was one small set of three drawers to store clothes, which was fine for three nights, but would have been difficult during a longer stay. At $158 per night (including tax) it was reasonably priced, but the age and the set-up of the rooms made it difficult to enjoy.  The room had various minor problems with it. The bathroom door wouldn鈥檛 close properly, which would have been fine, except that it would gradually drift open and had to be propped closed from the outside. The towel rack was starting to come out of its wall anchors, which gave the room a bit of a run-down look. In addition, the ice machine on our floor and the floor above did not work, so I was up two floors before I found one that did work. I was also disappointed by the hotel鈥檚 business center and internet service. On our last night, I asked whether there was somewhere I could check-in on-line for my flight home and print out boarding passes. They directed me to their business center. Not only did they charge $6 for 15 minutes of internet access, but they also charged for printing pages. The first two pages printed fine. But after I sent my third and fourth pages to the printer, I received a pop-up message indicating that I would be charged another dollar or so. The hotel鈥檚 wireless internet (which I accessed in my room) worked fine, but it is a pet peeve of mine that some hotels charge a daily fee for access. As a hotel guest, I shouldn鈥檛 expect to be charged for internet access any more than I should expect to be charged for towels or shampoo.  The SF Drake holds itself up as a classy, classic hotel. Unfortunately, it is becoming very close to being simply an old hotel. Despite the great location and the good price, I would probably look for somewhere else to stay next time.

<Author>KingH
<Content>Nice hotel Whilst staying with family in the Bay Area we spent a few days staying here in the city. The hotel was easy to locate and in a great central position for shops, trams, tourist spots and other amenities. Staff were helpful although as a Brit I must say that the beefeaters were unintentionally hilarious especially in the 90+F temperatures. Our room, though not huge, was perfectly comfortable and was well serviced. Ice/drinks machines on the corridor were a cheaper alternative to the minibar. Only complaint about the room was the noise from the AC and other rooms, which was mainly due to the fact that a woman next door came in late and screaming, knocking on doors. However a member of staff calmed her down and all other nights were fairly quiet. Our bathroom was also small but clean. The cocktail bar on the top floor was impressive and the full length gowns/tuxedo uniform was novel - the drinks was delicious too! The restaurant downstairs was fantastic and the breakfast very reasonable. The night that we dined there it was very busy and the food was probably the best we had on our trip. The huge Borders Bookshop across the road is a good place to waste time when waiting for you reservation time too! The left luggage service was efficient and check in and out was smooth and easy. I am also impressed to see the manager responding to many of the comments.

<Content>Great deal on a centrally located historic hotel My husband and I stayed at the Sir Francis Drake for two nights April 4-6, 2008. I've stayed in MANY San Francisco hotels around Union Square but have never stayed at the Sir Francis Drake -- probably because I thought it would be too touristy. <Author>Belasaria
<Content>Beautiful lobby, great location, but hit or miss with the rooms This was my second stay at the Sir Francis Drake, having stayed here in March 2008. My group was placed at the hotel by the housing bureau of the conference we were attending. The hotel's location is perfect for those wanting to get the feel of San Francisco. Close to the convention center, right in Union Square, with Chinatown only a few blocks away. For those who love to shop, there are plenty of stores.The doormen are dressed in costume and are quick to help with luggage and hailing taxis. The bellman are efficient and quick to point out the features of the room as well as where the ice machine and fire exits are.Check in was smooth and effortless, even when I forgot my Kimpton rewards number. The staff member kindly looked it up and added it to my reservation. The lobby of the hotel is magnificent, with high ceilings, comfortable sofas and chairs, and a nicely stocked bar. Aaron, one of the bartenders, is delightful and charming as well as creative. He was mixing up new drinks and explaining to the patrons the different tastes he was going for. There were a few of us there on business, so it was nice to have an engaging bartender. The elevators are small but relatively quick. During my first stay in March, I was on the 10th floor and had a decently sized room. The TV was on the dresser at the foot of the bed, so viewing wasn't an issue. The bathroom, however, was very small with little storage space for my toiletries. For a one-night stay, that's OK, but for the May trip, I was there for 7 days, so the lack of space became tedious.The bath amenities are Aveda products, which are my personal favorites. The tub is deep and the shower had good water pressure. For my second stay in May, I was on the 7th floor, close to the elevator. My room was tricky to get to, since it was tucked away in a side hall. The space was considerably smaller -- reminding me of a European hotel room -- and the TV was on the dresser that was parallel to the bed. Yes, viewing was a bit of a pain in the evening but it wasn't too bad.The real eyesore in the room was the left-over in-window AC/heating unit. The Sir Francis Drake now has central heating/air with individual temperature controls. While I didn't have a problem with mine, several of my colleagues complained that their AC didn't work. It, of course, had to be a freakish heatwave that hit in May, with temperatures well into the high 90's. Kudos for complimentary wireless internet access, but my telephone didn't work even after maintenance repaired it once. It's hard to order room service when the only phone in the room doesn't work.The business center is located in the lobby and has two pay-per-use computers. Unfortunately, the first computer I tried to use wouldn't recognize my memory stick and the printer connect to the second one constantly jammed. Of course, I was trying to print out documents for a meeting that was starting in 15 minutes. Three cheers for Elgin at the front desk, who tried to fix the printer and the understanding that I was under the gun, took the memory stick, printed the file and made the number of copies I needed. Because I had so much trouble with the machines, he didn't charge me for the copies. So... while my coworkers' experiences were particularly good, I didn't have problems with my room (except that the bathroom had no storage). It seems that it all depends on the luck of the draw with rooms. You'll either get one that has a decent amount of space or one that's cramped with things that don't quite work. Regardless, it is a beautiful hotel and I'm willing to stay here again as long as Aaron's at the bar and Elgin's behind the front desk.  
<Date>Jun 4, 2008

<Author>SD_based
<Content>a great value and exceptional service -- one of the best in the city! The Sir Francis Drake is managed by the Kimpton group and reflects that company's high standards of service. As with most downtown lodging, it is a *hotel* and not a *resort* in the comptemporary sense of the latter. That being said, there are a number of resort-like amenities available -- such as the spa, fitness center and business center.VALUE: If Union Square is your desired base of operations for your stay in San Francisco, the Sir Francis Drake offers some outstanding deals thourgh their online booking website. We were able to stay three nights for one-third the lowest rate offered by the Westin St. Francis just down the block. In this economy, that is a significant savings without giving up much in terms of luxury or amenities. LOCATION: You truly can't beat the location. a block up Powell Street from Union Square and all of the shopping that district has to offer. The cable cars stop right out in front of the hotel. The famous Dragon Gate entrance to Chinatown is walking distance four short blocks away.THE ROOMS: Ours was a 'Double Deluxe' with two very comfortable double beds. The room decor was very nice and fresh. The room itself was very clean and plenty large enough for my wife and I. Contrary to what others have written, the bathroom was every bit as large as you will find in most other three- and four-star hotels. If I were to have any concerns whatsoever about our room it was how few electrical outlets there were -- but I would only deem that a minor inconvenience.PEACE AND QUIET: Yes, the walls are somewhat thin and occasionally, we could hear the folks in the room next door trying to deal with their children. However, we did *not* hear the street noise others allude to. I suspect that is only an issue on rooms facing the street along the front of the building. Nor did we ever hear anything from the Starlight Room. Overall, it is a very quiet building for the most part.SERVICE: From the time we checked in and throughout our stay, every hotel staff member we interacted with was friendly and helpful. There was even a situation when we ran out of shampoo and called later in the evening to request an additional one from housekeeping. By this time, the housekeeping staff were not available, but in less than five minutes of calling guest services, shampoo was brought to our 7th-floor room by one of the building maintenance staff.FOOD: In addition to an excellent restaurant (Scala's Bistro) onsite, there are several dining options within a short walk. The famous Sears Fine Food restaurant (home of the Swedish pancakes) is directly across the street. Up on the corner is one of several downtown Lori's Diner locations. The Cheesecake factory is down the street atop Macy's Union Square store. Other eateries large and small abound.OTHER COMMENTS: Others had complained about slow and creaky elevators, but we rode all four and all were modern, quiet and efficient. Nothing to worry about there. We highly recommend the Sir Francis Drake and are planning to stay there again on our next visit to San Francisco.TRANSPORTATION TIP: If you are flying into San Francisco, skip the rental car unless you are going to be taking day trips outside of the city. Street parking is nearly non-existent and traffic tight in the central city and parking garages are expensive. Valet parking at the Sir Francis Drake was $44/day at the time of our visit. Instead, take BART (Pittsburg/Bay Point train) directly from the airport's international terminal to downtown (Powell Street station) and the hotel is 4陆 blocks up Powell. Stop by the Muni tranit kiosk next to the cable car terminus and buy a Muni 1-day or 3-day passport for unlimited cable car, streetcar, metro and bus rides

<Author>leahschatz
<Content>i was disappointed and room was dangerous Stayed at the hotel for a business conference and extended our stay to see sights and family in the area. Booked our stay through the Kimpton program and then confirmed the room and specific requests (crib, coffee pot, childproofing items) that were available to Kimpton members. Checkin was prompt and pleasant. Room on initial inspection was clean, nice decor and small bathroom with deep tub. We had to call multiple times for the crib and coffee pot over the next coupla hours before they were received. Childproofing items were never received. On our fouth night there the air conditioning broke. Early the next morning I informed the front desk of the problem. At lunch I reminded them again. That afternoon I called twice due to the room being too hot for the kiddos to nap. Room temperature exceeded 85 degrees. Still no maintenance service. Spoke to someone at the front desk again on the way out to dinner. After dinner, no one had looked at the room yet. Went back down to the front desk and let them know that I was very unhappy at this point. Twenty minutes later maintenance finally arrived. (It's now 9.30 pm and the 3 year old and 3 month old are hot and tired. We have an early flight home in the morning) Arturo,the maintenance man, fixed a pressure problem and left. An hour later the air conditioning quit working again. We decided it was hopeless at this point and decided to go to bed. My husband thought to check the window to see if we could get any fresh air. The window opened easily!! We had specificly been put in this room on the 11th floor to meet fire code with the crib. My 3 year-old son had spent a good portion of the time in the room sitting of the window sill looking out the window. He would've been able to easily open it. The other window was barely fasted close with a screw.I informed the front desk on the continued AC problems and the danger of the windows as we were quickly leaving for the airport. I love old hotels. I prefer the character and history of them to the mass-produced chains. This is the primary reason I selected this hotel. Hopefully, the problems will be promptly fixed. But personally, I have grave misgivings about staying somewhere where my child's life was in danger.

<Author>Bliss_Blister
<Content>Great Lobby Ok Rooms Classic lobby. You will be immediately impressed walking into the hotel (after you find it). Hotel is what you call a vintage location, the type of place you see in movies from the 40s. The bad news is rooms are small...really small, just like those old hotels. Walls are incredibly thin. I heard my neighbors alarms, showers and even snoring. Wireless is a plus. Didnt try the nice looking but expensive resturant or the number 1 in San Fran club on the top floor, but heard some negative reviews from people in the elevator on the way down. Keep in mind I was there midweek so maybe it picks up on weekends. Location is great, near union plaza, a few blocks from the BART. Great food choices close by but you will walk a couple of those steep San Fran blocks. I wasnt looking for fancy places just local type dinning and found Lori's and the Pizza place just north of the hotel to be great places for a leisurely dinner. Would stay here again but only as a 2nd or 3rd choice. Beware of panhandlers. The walk from the BART during the day and evening was filled with homeless and panhandlers. TONS! About 5 each block. Be careful.

<Content>Great Hotel; Great Location Stayed here for three nights in April with four friends - it was a great experience. Check-in was efficient and we were allowed to go straight to our rooms despite arriving well before the 3.00pm check-in time. I loved the reception area and lobby - it was very grandiose! The twin double room was spacious, clean and the beds were really comfortable. We had a great view of Union Square and Macy's. I loved the Aveda products in the bathroom and dressing gowns (one in tiger skin print, the other in zebra skin print!) were an added bonus! The hotel is in a superb location - lots of great diners (try Roxy's just up the street from the hotel), restaurants (try EO Trading Company around the corner), bars and caf茅s within 5 minutes walk; Chinatown 5 minutes walk and right beside Union Square and great shopping! Also, the cable car ($5 per ride) stops right outside the hotel and brings you out to all that is Fisherman's Wharf. We also spent two of our nights in the hotel's top floor bar - Harry Denton's Starlight Room - this has spectacular night time views of San Fran, a comprehensive cocktail menu, excellent service, live music, hopping DJs, a busy dancefloor and a great atmosphere. I hope to go back to SF and would absolutley definitely stay here again - I have already recommended it to family and friends intending to travel to SF and all of the above for a fantastic price!

<Author>kawh
<Content>Great Stay at the S.F.Drake - Kimpton Scores Again Ok. The windows are, indeed, filthy. I mean really, truly filthy on the outside. I will take on faith the explanation given earlier here on T.A. and not count it... but if I hadn't read it here first, it would have been a total turn-off when I arrived.... Having said that, we had a fantastic weekend stay here. First of all, the staff was very friendly and helpful. They helped us with directions, etc. etc. Always with a smile. They have done a nice job of redoing the rooms. The usual Kimpton tasteful decor. Ours was in the tower, with 2 double beds. We slept like babies. Perhaps because it is an older hotel, we heard no noise from neighbors at all. We were fairly close to the elevators and were worried, but it was never an issue. The bathroom was very small, but that's an old hotel for you. This is not a bathroom that can handle 2 people at the same time... but everything was clean and well maintained. They left more than enough towels... something I appreciate. The beds were great. Very firm. Just right for us. The sheets were wonderful. The top spread was covered top and bottom with clean white sheets. I love that. They are currently having a special for Hybrid cars. Vallet parking is FREE. That saved us, with tax, $100.00 for our 2 night stay... (typical downtown rate of $44.00 a night.) Lucky us! This hotel is the perfect location for shopping, theater, and exploring San Francisco. On top of it all, they accept dogs with no added (bogus) cleaning fee. It was the perfect hotel for a perfect weekend in San Francisco. I wouldn't want them to change a thing. (well.... ok... except the windows....)

<Author>cgstine33
<Content>The Drake is Great! I have read through the reviews of this hotel before writing mine and want to clarify a few things based on my stay. First, this is a boutique historic hotel. When we arrived we heard another guest complaining about the size of her room, and I want to say what did you expect? If you want a big boxy standard room, go to the Sheraton. This is why you stay at a place like the Drake, because the quirlky small rooms are charming! We had a king bed (luxurious) in a smaller sized room right near the elevator on the 12th floor. Because this is an old building we couldn't hear a thing outside our door. Not a problem at all with noise. The bedding was very high quality, definitely Kimpton standard. The decor in the room was also great - mismatching striped wallpaper and headboard - also a great quirky feature of a boutique hotel. And yes, the bath was small. Over three days I think we probably spent a total of 30 minutes in the bathroom - does the size really matter? The best part of this hotel is its location in Union Square on the cable car line. You really feel like you in the middle of it all, and it is a great starting point for getting all over the CIty (right near the Bart, Muni, Cable Car, etc.) Also, the dining in this neighborhood is fabulous. Our best restaurant experience was at a Mexican place (Colibri) recommended by the Concierge! We booked on Expedia and got a great three day mid-week rate of $100 a night. The ONLY complaint I have about the Drake is the heating/cooling system (apparently new) in the room. Our thermostat was inoperable and the room hovered between 75 and 80 degrees the whole time we were there. We called to complain twice and either had no response or the fix didn't work (we were out when they came). Because we are from Seattle, I think we were pretty ok with a warm room in spring, but it was mildly annoying. I would definitely recommend this hotel for the value. Definitely above average.  
<Date>Apr 10, 2008

<Author>agentlei
<Content>Quaint hotel, great locaton Loved this charming hotel! I'm a native San Franciscan now living in Las Vegas AND a travel agent for the last 10 years. This was the first time I have done the touristy thing in my own hometown as I was a tour guide for about 10 of my friends who have never been to the Bay area.The Sir Francis Drake is a landmark, perfect location to everythng.Service was great, rooms were nicely decorated- it was definitely a lovely hotel.Keep in mind that San Francisco is an old city with OLD buildings, most of the hotels downtown will be a little used and abused, however, they all do try to renovate to give clients nicer amenities without losing the old-fashioned feel of how San Francisco is supposed to be. Old Victorians, one way streets, rolling hills and old world charm- I never thought I would appreciate the history and architecture of San Francisco until I did not live here anymore...The Sir Francis Drake is the pefect embodiment of what Old San Francisco is supposed to be.I would stay here again and woud definitely recommend to my clients looking for a boutique hotel in San Francisco.

<Author>SeattleTraveler88
<Content>Good value. Great lobby. Fabulous location. Our family of five just spent three nights at the Drake. Although I was a bit concerned after reading TA reviews, I booked it anyway because the price was right. We had a king room on the 14th floor with two double beds, a pull out couch and a roll away for $248 including parking. This was very reasonable given the stellar location just off of Union Square and right on a cable car line. In addition, many of the other hotels I contacted would not allow a roll away to be added. At other hotels, we would have needed two separate rooms. In general, we were very happy with the room. We mostly appreciated the pillows. They were feather but not overstuffed like most. The mattresses were very comfortable. The room was still spacious even with the extra beds and very clean. The bedding, headboards, wallpaper and curtains are all new. The rest of the furniture was slightly worn but nothing horrible. Our only complaint was that we had difficulty regulating the room temperature. It was a bit warm so we just opened a window. We did not mention this to the front desk until checkout. It seems they have a new heating/cooling system and are still working out the kinks.If you like old, grand hotels, this is for you. The lobby is beautiful and ornate. However, the hotel is not fully renovated. Be preared for clean but dingy hallways once you get off the elevator. I asked the manager about future plans. They are upgrading their fitness center, then replacing windows and then renovating the hallways. On the plus side, the hotel restaurant, Scala, has great ambience and is excellent for dinner or a late night snack. We ate there twice. There is a Borders and a drug store (where you can buy multi day City Passes) just across the street. The cable car is right out front.The staff was very friendly and interested in our satisfaction with the exception of one of the doormen in Beefeater attire who was clearly dissinterested in answering our questions. In summary, we would definitely stay here again if the prices remain unchanged.  
<Date>Apr 6, 2008

<Author>markusinmiami
<Content>Nice, centrally located hotel The Sir Francis Drake is one of SF's 'grande dames' of hotels, which you can see by their lobby and their central location near Union Square. It also means that the hotel (particularly the hallways) is somewhat structurally outdated but the Kimpton group did a nice job renovating the rooms, incl. Aveda products and wifi-throughout the hotel. The service was very friendly. You should definitely check out the Starlight room on top for a drink with a view, and the close-by 'Crepe o Chocolat'-bistro for homemade organic foods (75 O'Farrel Street, one bloc south of Union Square)!

<Author>spider85
<Content>Loved the Sir Francis Drake! The SF Drake was wonderful! Its location cannot be beat for getting around the city and jumping on the cable car or walking over to Market St. to catch the new trains or over to Sutter for a bus. It is walking distance to many sights: Union Square shops, Yerba Buena Gardens and MOMA, the SF Center (now called Westfield) and of course, Chinatown. Our room was moderate in size...2 queen beds and a small bathroom, but was recently renovated and was clean and had a nice, stylish decor. I agree with what some have said about the windows...you really cannot see out of them because they are so dirty, but we were not in our rooms for much of the time and the view was not all that important to us. What we loved was the ambiance of the hotel...a charming, lovingly restored property that has a very friendly staff and provided all the ammenities we could have asked for. We traveled with our 2 young children and they loved the Beefeaters who stand guard the hotel and are happy to help or pose for photos. The lobby has a nice bar for meeting friends and having a drink. The hotel has an elegant feel without being too pretentious...it was comfortable and inviting. And, without doubt, the best location for getting around the Beautiful City by the Bay!!

<Author>LookitsJessica
<Content>Great Location! Definitelly "Historic" I have stayed at Kimpton hotels before so I thought Sir Francis Drake would be another name on my list of great stays. While I thought the location was wonderful, there were a few things to be desired. The porters were extremely helpful and friendly as well as the doormen. The great service stopped there. We wanted to attend the Sunday's a Drag event at the Starlight Lounge, but the concierge was unwilling to help us book a table. Instead of answering questions she told us to look in the guide in our room and call ourselves. We called the hotel befor we arrived to inquire about transportation from the airport. We were basically told to check online and figure it out.The rooms were very cute. I love the decorative style of the Kimpton brand. Our room looked as though there had been some water damage on one of the walls adjoining the bathroom that had been repaired, but not very well. The wall was bubbling out and was squishy. The free wireless internet was great. It made it easy for us to look up things to do and see. The hotel bar was beautiful and the drinks were great. The maid service was great, our room was cleaned very well. I love the doormens outfits and cheery disposition. I also noticed the dirty windows, but had read responses by the management about the reasoning. We spent little time in our room so that didnt bother me. Overall I thought that the hotel was beautiful. I just wish the service had been a little better.

<Content>Only worth it if the sleeping room rate is severly discounted Paid $169 p/night -- booked online through travel wholesaler (Expedia). It's an old hotel so some latitude needs to be extended in certain areas. We specifically asked for a room away from the elevator and we were placed RIGHT NEXT to the elevator in what was little more than a converted closet. Still, it is hardly the value I was seeking. Small cramped room, miniature bathroom but I nice big closet. The queue line is supposed to make the hotel guests feel like they are prioritized but it just makes it all the more ordinary. One more inconvenience in a city where choices are plentiful and the desire to ever return to the Sir Francis Drake becomes non-existent.Too bad that they cannot capitalize on their history in a manner that would make a guest want to return.

<Author>frangipani7
<Content>Generally pleasant experience; good value for the money My husband and I were in San Francisco to visit relatives and stayed for 3 nights at the Sir Francis Drake. At $99/night, I can't rate too harshly. The hotel pretty much met our expectations - somewhat old and faded, but offering a decent standard of accommodation and service.The man at check-in was very nice and gave us a triple upgrade in room class. So goodness knows what were were supposed to get for our $99. We ended up with a corner room on the 16th floor that had something of a city view, although it was mostly blocked by the 'utility terrace' outside the windows. (There were satellite dishes, cables, tarps, etc on this 'terrace' - more on that later).The room had been pretty recently renovated, not using the finest materials and craftsmanship, but well enough to make it cheerful. The bed was comfortable and we were happy with the room temperature. The bathroom was modern but tiny. We had a tub and shower, no problems with water pressure, although we did have trouble with a broken sink stopper. Our biggest complaint was the windows. They are old and we were in San Francisco on a rainy and windy weekend. The windows rattled all night long, and the tarps on the 'terrace' outside our room blew like flags unfurling all night long. We live in Manhattan, in a prewar apartment overlooking a major avenue, and this was the noisiest night we've ever spent. The windows definitely need to be replaced!We didn't spend much time at the hotel, but the staff members we interacted with were friendly and competent. For $99/night, I definitely feel we got our money's worth.

<Author>xp01321
<Content>Lame excuses and system failures Stayed at the Sir Francis Drake for two nights last week. I have used several other Kimpton hotels, and they have all been very enjoyable stays, so my expectations were reasonably high when we checked in.After two nights at this hotel, I can only say that this hotel must be the exception to the Kimpton brand of hotels and their excellent service and ambience overall. When we entered our room, we could not see through the window, neither could we shut it properly. It looked as if the window had not been cleaned since the hotel opened for business in the 1920's. When I told the front desk about this, they claimed that the hotel is undergoing renovations and therefore the windows are dirty. In addition, the windows had been recently cleaned (!), and were due to be replaced soon. Pardon my ignorance, but there was absolutely no information on this in my room, and there was nothing to indicate ongoing renovations.Another thing that irritated me is that the front desk failed to wake-up me at 6 am, although we had asked for this specifically, since we were catching an early flight. The front desk feed-back was: Yes, your request is in our system, but the framework does not work. I asked again, and was told that in plain English, the internal hotel system for wake-up calls was not working. Lucky for us, I woke up a few minutes before 6 o'clock and we made it to the airport in time.Finally, I used the business centre to access the Internet. The exorbitant rate of 23.80 USD per hour is very steep in my view, particulalrly since the two computers I used did not work. I was still being charged the full price. When I asked an agent at the front desk, I was told that the computers are managed by a third party, and guess what, I had experienced another system failure.In conclusion, I think Kimpton is a great hotel chain, and this particular hotel has an unbeatable location. That being said, I would strongly suggest to stay clear of this hotel. To be fair, we were offered a 15 % discount, but I still left the hotel with a bad taste in my mouth.

<Author>AEC in SF
<Content>Stylish -- almost luxurious We chose the Sir Francis Drake as an alternative to staying home during a neighbor's all-night party, so all we really needed was a quiet, comfortable place to sleep where we could also bring our dogs. The room was stylish, although certainly not luxurious. Even though we chose a Tower Queen room (an upgrade from Queen Petite and Queen Standard) our room was on the small side. There was plenty of room to move around, and even a large desk, but one side of the bed was up against the wall (no end table). The bathroom was well-appointed but truly tiny -- you basically have to sit at an angle on the toilet to keep from impaling yourself on the TP holder -- although at least we had a tub/shower (most room categories apparently don't). It felt like a NYC hotel bathroom.It took more than an hour, two phone calls, and a visit to the lobby to finally get a dog bed and bowls to use during our stay -- which we were offered when we checked in. None of the employees seemed to know where they were, or who to ask. Kimpton hotels pride themselves on being pet-friendly, I would have expected better. We were exhausted and just wanted to get to sleep, but we were unable to do so because we had to wait up for the bellman to bring these items.If you're travelling with pets -- who might be over-excited by the noise and festivity of the lobby bar on Friday night -- you can enter off the Sutter Street side of the building and take the elevator from the lower lobby straight up to your room.

<Author>KM37
<Content>Fantastic location, great service My husband and I stayed here for 3 nights in January and were very pleased. We arrived early Friday (11:30am), so our room wasn't quite ready, but by the time we grabbed some lunch and came back we were able to check in. The staff was very courteous and helpful. Requests for a heating pad and extra pillows were answered within 5 minutes. The room was clean and cozy, and plenty big enough for the two of us. The bathroom needs additional shelving space to put toiletries since the vanity is small. It would have been nice to unpack those items rather than have to keep them in the beside drawer. The bed was comfortable, and the shower head was great for tall people. We never had to wait more than a few minutes for the elevators. One quibble is we were not able to get the room cool enough for our liking while sleeping. It would only go down to 66 degrees, and I am not sure that it really was that cool in the room. We would have opened the windows while we slept to get it a bit cooler, but there are not screens and I didn't want a stray bird wandering in. For most people, not getting the room cool enough in January is probably not a concern.The location is terrrific. We bought a 7-day Muni pass for $24 and did not need to rent a car. The cable car stop is right outside the front door, or, it is a short walk to Market street to catch a trolley car or bus. The location of the hotel is by far the biggest asset. There is so much shopping, dining, and activity all around. We would definitely stay here again on our next trip to San Francisco.

<Author>ss77
<Content>Location, Location, Location Great location. Highly recommend staying in Union Square as opposed to Fisherman's Warf. It only took us a couple hours to be bored and done with Fisherman's Warf. This hotel was a great location. It is a little noisy (and we were on the far side from the trolleys on the 11th floor). However, we actually enjoyed the street noise and trolley bells as it added to the feel of being in San Francisco. The room is small, but we went with the deluxe room and it was well worth the money. Most importantly, the room and hotel were clean and in nice condition and the bed was comfortable. I would recommend this hotel. A tip to save some money - park in the sutter-stockton garage (in the quad between sutter, stockton, bush and grant streets). In is a short block and a half walk and saves considerable money compared to the valet only offered by the hotel.

<Author>bmacbc
<Content>accentuate the positives... My partner and I had the opportunity to stay at the Sir Francis Drake just after Christmas for three nights, where we were joined by my mother-in-law. The hotel is conveniently situated in the heart of Union Square, next to all the fantastic shopping that surrounds it. The hotel is charming from the beefeaters at the door, to the grand foyer and lobby. It is out of a different era.We had booked an Executive King for ourselves (room 925)and a regular Queen for the mother-in-law. Upon check-in, I was pleasantly surprised to see how big our room was. I believe that two rooms had merged to create a larger suite. The interior designers have had a lot of fun decorating the rooms. They are very unusual and kitschy, but at the same time stylish. Our room had a couch and chair, desk, king bed, bar fridge, tv, etc... all the usual touches. The only thing missing was an in-room safe and coffee maker.The bathroom was large with both a shower stall and a tub, but had a small vanity which made it hard to place all our bath products. The hotel supplies Aveda products so the quality was high. The bathroom decor fit the period style of the hotel, but was recently updated. There were a couple of problems with our room... the biggest being its location. All the executive kings face Powell Street, which you will soon find out to be a bustling thoroughfare that is busy from morning to midnight. The clang clang clang of the trollies and other street noise will most likely keep some guests up at night. (they offer earplugs at the front desk, which I took advantage of.) I wouldn't recommend this side of the hotel for people who can't handle street noise. And there are other noises beyond that... early morning garbage trucks... and drunks leaving the Starlight Room... One minor problem was the dirty windows in our room that you could hardly see out of... I am not kidding... it looked like years of dirt and dust... the windows in this room were still single pane, so this might be a reason for the noise, too.My favorite part about the room was the bed... It is very comfortable.My mother-in-law had a much smaller room on the back side of the building... and it seemed much quieter. This room was small by anyone's standards... with one of the most claustrophobic bathrooms I have ever seen. I kid you not, but you almost have to sit on the toilet to brush your teeth or do your makeup. You might have two square feet of leg room. I wouldn't recommend the queen room for more than one person... and never for a big person... There is no room to move.All in all we had a good stay. I would recommend making sure you get the right room for yourself. The executive king was great but there was the noise factor... I wouldn't want the smaller room. But if all you want is a good comfortable bed, then go for it. The SFD's location can't be beat, with everything at your doorstep and the staff is friendly.I would recommend this hotel, but with a few caveats... but I would stay here again if the price was right. I have stayed at other Kimpton hotels in the past and this one seems just a step below... but the hotel has a certain grandeur to it that you won't get in a boutique hotel. I would have given it four stars had it not been for the noise...  
<Date>Jan 2, 2008

<Author>dephal
<Content>Overall, positive experience I just spent 1 night at the Drake with my mother and my 8-year-old daughter. I got a very good rate, although valet parking will add another $50/night to the cost.There were a few minor snags with our stay. It was quite busy in front of the hotel when we pulled up, and it took several minutes to get the attention of someone to help with the car. We removed our luggage ourselves. Our room wasn't ready, which was no big deal because it was only 11 am, several hours before check-in time. We stowed our luggage and went off into the city. When we returned several hours later and checked in, it took a really long time--over half an hour--for someone to bring our luggage up. And even though I'm a Kimpton In-Touch member (which was acknowledged when we checked in) there was no welcome amenity in the room. So I called down and they did bring one later.The good points outweighed the bad. The staff were all very friendly, and someone called the room about 6:30pm just to make sure everything was okay. The lobby is spectacular. The room itself, a queen-queen tower room, was clean and nicely decorated and had a great view (though the outside of the windows badly need washing!). The beds were very comfortable and the room itself quiet. And the location is fabulous. Union square is right down the block, and Chinatown and several museums are within easy walking distance. If you want to wander farther afield in the city, public transportation is easy to get to. And what could beat lying in your bed on a foggy night and listening to the cable cars clanging 17 floors beneath you?

<Author>sunchaser576
<Content>Great hotel; great location My husband and I stayed at the Sir Frances Drake Hotel for two nights just before Christmas to celebrate my birthday, and had a very enjoyable visit. This was my first time staying at the hotel. our room was a King Delux, and while the room was not huge, it was plenty big enough for us with stylish decorations and good quality bed linens. The bathroom was a good size and the Aveda products were a nice touch. The hotel is in a lovely old building with a grand lobby with lots of character. But what really made our stay special was the staff. Everybody from the Beef Eaters and the bell boys to the front desk was friendly and helpful. When we arrived the bell boy helping me with our luggage told me to ask at the desk for Macy's coupons before going shopping. We called room service for robes and they were at the door almost immediately. When we went to the fabulous Starlight Room for a cocktail the host was exceptionally nice and made us feel both welcome and special, and because we told him we had dinner reservations elsewhere he made sure that our server was aware that we had a time constraint. Kudos to whoever is responsible for staff training.I have stayed at far more expensive hotels in this country and abroad, but rarely have had such consistently good service. I will definitely stay at the Sir Frances Drake again.

<Author>sanfranmanPhoenix_Az
<Content>Okay, but not as promised. I stayed at the Sir Francis Drake December 14 -16. I was advised of a $99.00 promo rate on Travelzoo, and was directed to the Kimpton Hotels website to book the room. Because the promo rate didn't come up on the Kimpton website, instead showing a $119 rate as the promo rate, I called a reservationist on the toll free number and was told that the $99 rate was sold out. However, the reservationist told me that the $119 rate (also a promo rate) was for an upgraded deluxe room on a higher floor in the tower section of the hotel. When I checked in, I was given a room on the 9th floor -- not a higher floor. The room had to be a standard room. It certainly was not deluxe. Although the hotel staff were pleasant, it was difficult to get the concierge to answer when dialing from the room. Additionally, the bathroom was tiny as was the closet. The wallpaper, though stylish, was peeling from the wall in places. The window -- the outside at least -- was so dirty that it was difficult to see through the dirt. All of the above aside, the hotel is very well located and a great example of 1920s hotel architecture. Also, the room was clean and the bed was comfortable.

<Author>t_rose72
<Content>Great Location, Nice Amenities A friend and I came to SF to do some shopping and to see all the holiday decorations around Union Square. It was great just walking around, it was so pretty at night with all the trees and lights! The hotel's location is very ideal, as it's basically right next to Union Square. The decor of the lobby is beautiful. We got a Queen Petite Room and the name of it is spot on. It's fairly small. We didn't mind since we weren't in the room that much. The room was clean and the Aveda products are a plus.The Starlight Room on the 21st floor is pretty cool for the view and the dancing though a little pricey for drinks. The lobby bar was not crowded like others have posted but it was a Sunday. There's a bartender there that won best bartender in SF I guess. He was nice and seemed to have a local following. I also heard the drag show at the Starlight on Sunday afternoons are fun to see, but we missed it by 1/2 hour.What would make this hotel even better though is if the staff was really friendly. The service was really just okay overall. Check-in was good. but it actually seemed a bother to get help on a couple of occasions with directions, to get our luggage or to get restaurant recommendations. As some of these employees are the first people customers encounter, I would think the hotel would strive for exceptional service out of them.Luckily, the price and location overshadowed the service. We got a great rate for the room. At that price and being so close to Union Square, I think we would definitely stay at the Sir Francis again.

<Author>Rifle762
<Content>You Could (Should) Not Ask For More My wife and I stayed at the Sir Francis Drake for three days beginning the Friday after Thanksgiving. We chose the hotel based on: location, price and reviews. What a happy surprise our choice turned out to be! One half block to Union Square for the lighting of a huge Christmas Tree! Just pure luck on our part. Directly on the Powell-Hyde St. cable car, Union Square entertainment, shopping, restaurants, etc.etc.etc. You could throw a rock in any direction and hit more good restaurants than I have ever experienced in New Orleans. Great service. Every question was met with a smile and courtesy. Prompt friendly bell service and free room upgrade. Super decor, restaurant and night club atop the hotel with tremendous views. While waiting for our table at Scala's Bistro, which is in the hotel, the hostess walked out of the restaurant, up the stairs to the lobby, and found us at the bar to tell us our table was ready, all with a smile. Its a great old hotel in the city center; built years ago so expect the bathrooms to be smaller than you would wish for. I said small, not inadequate.Some tips: use public transportation while staying here. You have direct access to cable cars and buses and parking is too expensive. My best tip is to call the Muni phone number any time you want a bus or cable car. They will tell you exactly when and where to stand to catch your transportation and you get a human to talk to. Please take the 9x bus through China Town going to Fisherman's Warf. You really experience China Town that way! Free airport shuttle would make this hotel a 10.
