<Author>Retired1811
<Content>The Drake is Great! My wife and I did a four day trip to San Francisco to take in a few baseball games and the City. We have been to SF several times and stayed at various places around the city. I found a great rate at the Sir Francis Drake on their web site and reserved a room. Great rate and no money up front. The Drake is a fine classic hotel in the perfect location. The staff is extremely friendly and helpful. The rooms are a bit small, but all have been refurbished and are quite comfortable. Since SF is a great walker town, a right turn out of the front door leads to three straight blocks up, up and up before you start going down, down, down towards Fisherman鈥檚 Wharf. Excellent way to wear off breakfast. For those who want to pass on the walk, the classis cable car line goes right in front of the Drake, so just hop on! The light rail train to the ball park is a short 6-8 blocks away and a great, cheap way to get there. The staff at the Drake arranged for a rental car (Napa Valley trip) that was picked up and returned within 6-8 blocks from the Hotel. Very convenient in a city that is hell to drive in. We both highly recommend the Sir Francis Drake.

<Author>superstardj
<Content>A real mixed bag Sir Francis Drake hotel is a difficult one to review for me, as it did some things brilliantly, and some things rather badly.Let's start with the positives. The location is great. The rooms are lovely - very modern and stunningly themed, as you'd expect from a Kimpton hotel. The room service food (served from the Bistro downstairs) was possibly the best ever food I have had delivered to my room - I had a stunning pan-seared salmon fillet one night and a house pasta the next, both amazing. It's rare for me to get excited about room service food, but this was really, really good.Onto the negatives, and this mainly relate to the service: the staff just weren't as accomodating / helpful as they could have been - perhaps they're taking the olde English aristocratic thing a bit too seriously? Upon checking in, we first had an issue where our booking reference wasn't being accepted - and the receptionist rather patronisingly suggested we had the wrong hotel and attempted to direct us to another hotel of a similar name nearby. After insisting that we were in the right place, he checked with a more knowledable colleague who explained to him that the number I was giving him was from some sort of central reservations system, and hooray, our booking was found. Not a great start. Then, despite the fact that our rooms had already been paid for, the receptionist attempted to put a hold on $900 on my credit card, the cost of the rooms (despite the fact a third party had already covered their cost), plus $100 per night incidentals. I explained that I didn't understand why this had to be done, as our the cost of our stay had already been paid for, but his system insisted on doing it that way. Unhappy with him putting $900 on hold on my credit card I eventually just gave a cash deposit of $100 for each night, and we evenutally checked in, after about half an hour.That was the biggest issue, hence my still fairly high rating. We just felt on occasion the hotel staff didn't really make things as easy for us as we'd expect in a hotel of this calibre. That said, the rooms are gorgeous inside, and I would definitely stay here again.

<Author>the-rach
<Content>Love the Drake! We stayed at the Drake for 4 nights in September. I was slightly worried before we got there because we were due to arrive in the evening after a very long journey from the UK. I was very pleased with what we found. Check in was quick and easy, the room was extremely comfortable and charming, the shower was brilliant. I really can't think of anything to complain about! I'm very suprised there are negative reviews on here, but then they seem to be mainly about individual rooms. Ours was on the 3rd floor and we had no real problems at all. We found the staff to be really friendly and helpful, they booked our tickets to Alcatraz for us and gave us plenty of maps and directions. The location was fantastic. There are shops and restaurants nearby, and right outside you can get the tram down to the pier. I would recommend doing this once, but after that there is a very good bus service which is faster and cheaper. I worked out the bus routes from a map I got from the hotel lobby. We had breakfast once at the caffe espresso directly next door, which was very nice, and also once at Sears across the road (make sure you're hungry!). Over all, I would definitely recommend the Drake to others as a good budget hotel. I'm really glad we stayed there. And I love San Francisco! p.s loved the beefeaters too!

<Author>wcswing158
<Content>Honeymoon The Sir Francis Drake met my expectations from what I read from other reviews. It is an old hotel with a lot of character. It is centrally located in the Union Square area. It is within walking distance of Union Square shpping and attactions. We had a Queen Deluxe room (the bed was a king so we may have had an upgrade). It was reasonably large with a walk-in closet. The room decor was very nice. There was some cracked paint on the ceiling but this did not bother us (it added to the hotel's character). Based on other reviews, I expected this and think cracked paint is pretty common. The rooms were otherwise clean and in good order. The bed was very comfortable.The cable cars stop in front of the hotel but they are often full before they reach this stop. If we were going to the Fisherman's Warf, we would walk to Market street and take a street car. It is much easier to catch cable cars on the return trip. The Starlight Room is a nice nightclub with great city views. Contrary to other information I received, the dress code is now casual, and a jacket and tie are no longer required.

<Author>voreezz73
<Content>Great location, historical hotel, but not luxury The Drake鈥檚 high points are its location a 陆 block off Union Square and the historical beauty of the hotel evident in the ornate lobby and dramatic exterior. Check-in was just fine and the staff was polite and professional. But who goes to a hotel to hang out in the lobby? We had a queen corner room on the 18th floor with a gorgeous view of Union Square and the Westin St. Francis. The bed was a comfy pillow top and the smallish bathroom with new porcelain and marble finishes had Aveda products and served its purpose. A large person may find the bathroom a bit cramped. I suppose that some these flaws could be expected in an old hotel, but the missed details prevent the Drake from being a true place of luxury.

<Content>Great value for the money... I was a bit skeptical about heading to San Francisco... I wanted to be near my conference, but didn't want to spend that much to stay AT that hotel... Plus, I'm a smoker. San Francisco is pretty much a non-smoking city, including most of the hotels. Bummer.Fortunately, my request was honored - the hotel has ONE last floor that is smoking (which one of the front desk guys mentioned they were considering getting rid of it), but I can't tell you how stoked I was to be able to smoke in my room (advice to mgmt of SFD - there is a market for allowing smokers to honestly smoke in their rooms. 99% of the hotels in your city won't let it happen, but personally I will pay more for the privelege. Just a thought).My room was two double beds- I would have prefered a king, but oh well. The bathroom was a bit small but not a big deal. Good use of the space, at least. Large closet, free wifi, free coffee until 6:30am (after which I could buy coffee in the cafe), all-in-all I was very impressed with the hotel, the location and how nice all the staff was. I can't say that I've had any other experiences at all with hotels in this city, but unless they eliminate the smoking floor, I'm certain I'll be back.

<Author>bsb616
<Content>Great hotel, great location, disappointing service For the price and location, the Sir Francis Drake was probably the best value I've had at a hotel. It is steps from the Powell Street BART station, the cable cars and bus routes. It is also right at Union Square and surrounded by great shops and restaurants. The rooms are small, but keep in mind it is a major metropolitan city, and the rooms are usually small to accommodate all the people staying. While small, they were not uncomfortable in any way and were kept very clean. The only downfalls we experienced were small inconveniences from poor service. Hotels that master the art of the little things are always the best. This hotel is still working on mastering the little things. For instance, we had three people in the rooms and were there for 5 nights. On only one occasion were there three sets of towels. We had to call every time and they would bring giant stacks of towels. Unnecessary. They would also take the drinking glasses and not replace them. And we also received a bit of condescension when we left our boarding pass information they promised to book as the flight opened to get the A passes. We called 20 minutes to remind and it had not been done and we ended up getting stuck in a different boarding group. While some of the service issues were frustrating, it all comes out in the wash with a charming hotel with great period details and a perfect location and reasonable price.

<Author>brindare
<Content>A Terrible Disappointment Let me just start by saying that this was our first trip to San Francisco. My husband and i decided to ditch the East Coast when it came to our vacation this summer and go to Sunny California. I had some expectations of this hotel, but not to many given the fact that i had spoken twice to their Concierge, Ken prior to our arrival and both times he was dismissive and rude. I was trying to arrange some activities prior to our arrival and he told me that i didn`t need to book anything in advance ( never mind the fact that i didn`t want to spend my vacation planning my daily activities, hence i was trying to do it in advance) and when I asked about different tour companies that organized day trips outside of San Francisco, he described one of them and let me know that it was for outdoorsy people( you think?) and he didnt care much for being in the car for 3 hours on the way to the American River. I actually thought about moving our reservation to another hotel, but it was too late.The hotel itself is very old, but it does have a lot of charm. The lobby has somewhat of a feeling of grandeur but the years of neglect can easily be noticed. The check-in was pleasant, the Front Desk interaction being amongst the few pleasurable ones we had while we were there. The room was very small and very contrasting in what the decor and upgrades were concerned ( the Front Desk upgraded us at check-in because our room was not ready- i didn`t want to see the room we were initially in if THIS was an upgrade). The room had new curtains, new headboard ( with some very suspicious stains on it), a large flat screen TV, 1 night stand, 1 desk and chair. The bathroom seemed remodeled ( new vanity and commode) until you pulled back the shower curtain and you saw the old stained, chipped bathtub. Overall cleanliness- OK Anyway, the room was less important because we spent most of the time sightseeing.The Concierge Staff at the hotel was still rude and dismissive during our stay so we tried to stay clear of them and on our departure day we called 4 times to arrange for transportation to the airport, left a Voicemail and never heard back from them. Every time we would call the Hotel Operator to let them know that we were trying to get a hold of the concierge and they kept transferring us to the same extension that we had already called and that nobody answered. We finally went downstairs and we were informed by a patronizing Ken( same one as above ) that arranging airport transportation required for us to be physically present at his desk ( which no one had mentioned during our repeated transfer calls) and that he was extremely busy right as he walked in so he had not yet been able to return our call ( although when we arrived at his desk he was not even there and we had to ask the FD to get his from the back area).The conclusion.... I haven`t stayed at any other hotels in San Francisco but I the next time i`m in SF i will gladly try another one. Sir Francis Drake was not bad, and certainly the physical imperfection could have been overlooked if the staff was spectacular. But...

<Author>aarcher
<Content>BEWARE!!! THIS HOTEL HAS THEFT PROBLEMS!!! The rooms are small and the cleanliness was about average; just about what you'd expect for the price in San Francisco. We were fine with this, until we left our room on the 2nd day and returned to discover that our camera had been stolen. On our way out later that evening, we overheard a member of the hotel staff admonish a bellman because 3 bags had been stolen that day as well. When I reported the the theft to the management, I was told that their insurance company would contact me. Six weeks later, and after about a dozen requests for help, the insurance company told me they were denying my claim. The hotel acknowledged that someone using another key did enter the room that day (not to clean it, though...it was never cleaned that day), but since I couldn't remember exactly what time I returned (it was SIX WEEKS LATER), they wouldn't pay my claim. My advice would be to steer clear of this hotel. There are plenty of other good hotels in the area, and I'm betting their management is a little more careful with their guests' property.

<Author>a.p.1017
<Content>I can't believe the reviews are this bad... Went for a girls night out thing this past weekend and I stayed in a 2-queen room - it overlooked Union Square from one side and the Embarcadero from the other. The beds were incredible, and the furnishings and bathroom were great. Service was excellent, amenities were nice, and they left a little welcome amenity for us. The noise level in the room was good - unlike a lot of San Fran hotels it's nice and quiet at night. Went to the Starlight Room at the top of the hotel and had an absolute blast - live band, luxurious surroundings, but somehow the atmosphere managed to be comfortable and friendly. The worst I can say about this place? Well it's an old hotel and in some instances the halls are narrow. There are some places where the paint on the walls bleeds in to the ceiling. But the good things about this place more than make up for the little detractions. I think the hotel is under new management and has just completed renovations - I think the reason it's rated so low is it was formerly under poor management. All I know is it's one of the best deals on Union Square and it's also really nice - way better than the Hotel Union Square and I'd also say nicer than the Diva, and more whimsical and comfortable than the Park Hyatt, and more personal than the Hilton. Out of those four (which I've stayed at recently), I'd choose the Sir Francis Drake again above everything else - it's the best value.

<Author>larsthorwald
<Content>Four Days at the Sir Francis Drake Just returned from 4 days with my son's 7/8th grade class at the Sir Francis Drake hotel.It is in a great location for walking to Union Square, the Metreon, Chinatown and the really nice Mall opposite Powell Cablecar/Muni train/Bart Station.The staff is helpful and one evening there was even complimentary wine/nuts in the lobby around 6 pm. The view bar on the top floor was filled with really nicely dressed, really young people and there was 80's disco music playing! We went in for one drink, $10 and a $5 cover charge on a Thursday night!As with all old hotels the rooms are pretty small as are the bathrooms, but the carpet was new, the bed, nice and the linens were very good. Nice puffy duvets; no plastic blankets. You could not open the windows though.The ice machine on my floor did not work, so I had to call the desk every time I wanted ice. The heating/cooling system was a little quirky, but maybe that was because I did not know how to work it! My phone, a cordless, kept losing it's charge so one evening I had to call the desk for my ice on my cell! Someone came right up and fixed it though. Also my mini bar fridge never really got cold.The room was booked through our school;I gave them a check for over $600 for 3 nights, I assume they got a group rate. So I think it's a pretty average deal for the money.All in all I would recommend staying there even though I wish there was a little market nearby. It's close to transportation and the staff is very friendly.

<Author>SanDiegoAdventurer
<Content>Unbelievable customer service I stayed at the Sir Francis Drake with my fiance and my three children. We arrived very late on a Friday night (after midnight). Knowing that their room service closed at 10:00 p.m., I called earlier that day and made arrangements for non-perishable food to be left in our room. When we arrived, tired and hungry, the food was nicely laid out in the room as requested.While the hotel is older, the rooms are very comfortable and clean. The lobby is beautiful and the staff was polite and helpful.Unfortunately, my 9-year old daughter came down with the flu and was extremely ill when the time came to clean up the room and check out. Several hours after checkout, we realized that she had left her Nintendo DS, with all the games and carrying case, in the room. I immediately called the hotel and informed them of this situation. I followed up both in person and by telephone, but the hotel was unable to find the Nintendo. I therefore e-mailed the manager of the hotel explaining the situation to her. She launched her own investigation of the disappearance of the Nintendo -- to no avail. Then, to my surprise and the extreme pleasure of my daughter, Ms. Kershner informed me that the hotel would pay to replace my daughter's system. I informed her of the cost of the system and the games, and several weeks later, a check for that amount (plus some truffles, yum) came via Federal Express.This experience made my entire family a HUGE fan of the Sir Francis Drake Hotel!

<Author>LovesTheCity
<Content>Great Hotel In Central Location My husband and two sons (ages 9 and 11) stayed here for three nights during Spring break. It's a beautiful historic building and the rooms, though cozy, are very nicely appointed. The doorman in his Beefeater uniform was very friendly and helpful and the Concierge was also very helpful. Parking is pricy ($45) per night for the valet, but anything in this location is bound to be. I loved the historic interior decor. My only complaint is that our 8th floor window was very dirty. Ask for an upper room. From the higher floors the noise from outside is just a pleasant city hum. From the lower floors, the constant ding-ding of the cable car could be annoying. On the plus side, there is a cable car stop right in front of the hotel. Also, the location is great if you like to walk to things like Union Square and Chinatown. Don't miss Sears Fine Foods just across the street. Really liked this hotel.

<Author>TxTravelPro
<Content>Mini-Accomodations in a fine old building Stayed for 1 night and went to an event in a meeting room on the 2nd floor.Flew in to SFO and took BART into the city.$5.15 and just much easier and faster than you may think, practically door to door. Checked in at noon without problems. Front desk was very nice.They assigned me room 1232. Ran up to the room to dump my stuff and was surprised at the size of the room. Tiny. Maybe 8x14.The bathroom was in miniature too. Sink and toilet facing each other with about 18 inches between them and the bathrub ran the length, about 2 inches from the sink and toilet. Really small.In the bedroom, there was a full size bed, 2 small bedside tables, desk, chair and console with a TV and minibar.I don't mind small rooms when I travel alone, so the size did not bother me at all... It was just that I had only seen a hotel room this tiny once before (at the W on Lexington in NYC).Now, on to the funkiness of the hotel. It was pretty funky. The bed was clean and the table tops and such were clean but the walls were really nasty and the carpet was this very dark purple-y brown color. It did not look dirty... It was so dark I felt it must be dirty. The walls looked as if someone shook a hot can of coke and spewed it all over. The bed was pretty comfy but the pillows were both very firm.I ran down to the lobby to find a place for a quick bite. I stopped by the concierge and asked for a good sushi place and he recommended a place on Cyril Magnan (sp). I told him that was a little further than I wanted to walk right at the moment and was there anything good within a block. Keep in mind that there are probably 20 restaurants within a block. He turned into a [--] and rattled off 5 places in a second and when I repeated the only one I understood he said yeah, but its not that good. He was just very hateful. Kind of miserable. I was the only person there and there was no reason for him to get nasty when I ask for something a little closer. I mean, is a 2nd question too much to ask a concierge? Argh.So, I decided to go to the diner directly across the street. Sears is a good old fashioned diner. It's always good but the food is quite heavy and unhealthy... tasty though. I went to the event and thought the catering and event planning was good. The appetizers were good. Nice staff. Pretty meeting room.Then we headed to the sushi place recommended earlier, Hana Zen. Maybe it was an off night... pretty presentation, but only OK.Back to the hotel... Got ready for bed, took a shower where there was pretty low pressure. The tub is pretty long (maybe 5 or 6 feet) and deep. It was much better suited for a bath... which I decided to do. I cleaned it a little (just in case) then relaxed and read a magazine. It was nice.Check out the next morning at 930am and walked back to the BART station.San Francisco is beautiful. I wish I could have stayed longer... This hotel is in a wonderful location and I would stay here again if the price was right.

<Author>innkeepmendo
<Content>Great location - Clean - Classy This hotel is located right downtown in the Union Square area, very close to great shopping and dining. We stayed in a queen room which was surprisingly small. Very little extra room for anything, such as large suitcases or the in-room yoga program the hotel advertised. <Author>LAguy2000
<Content>Don't do it!!!!! The great location can't make up for this really badly run hotel. The first night we had to wait in line to use the elevator to get to our room -- there is a very popular nightclub on the 21st floor. There was no security at the elevator, and we didn't want to cut in front of already drunk people to get to our room. We were then kept up for hours by a whining window fan/AC. The next morning at 8am we were awakened by hammering. They moved us for the next night -- I immediatle tried the window a/c -- and it too was noisy. But on high it was quiet-ish. After waiting in line that night for our elevator again, we got to our room with a party going on next door. We turned on the fan (on high, of course) to drown them out. It was fine for a couple of hours, then started sounding like a car fan hitting a radiator. We tried sleeping with it off, but the street noise reverberates inside the a/c units and you hear every noise. I walked down at 3am to talk to the front desk. I was polite, but said I didn't think that this should be a problem paying over $200.00 a night for a room. He clicked on his computer and sniffed, through Expedia. Yes, through Expedia, but I STILL paid over $200 a night! On the plus side, they gave us free ear plugs. They say they're renovating, and the window fans are going, but that doesn't stop the elevator lines. And anyone who thinks it's acceptable to rent (very expensive!) rooms to people with malfunctioning equipment cannot be trusted.

<Author>bcfcfan
<Content>Nice Hotel in good location We are a family of three from England who spent seven nights at the Drake from 21st October. Having read previous grim reviews we were a little apprehensive but needn't have been . We found the hotel suited our holiday needs perfectly. However, we did email the hotel beforehand to request a refurbished room .The bedroom on 17th floor was of good size with two comfortable double beds and appeared recently decorated. The bathroom, although small was adequate and again very clean and well supplied with towels, toiletries etc. Staff when needed were always polite and efficient - in fact one day when maid forget to renew towels these were delivered to our door wthin five minutes of speaking to reception. Good views from the room but the windows were in desperate need of a clean (the only niggle we had). Would recommend both Sears and Lori's diner nearby for breakfast. As for location - it couldn't be bettered - easy walking distance to Union Square, Chinatown and other sights plus a cable car ride (stop outside hotel) to the bay.

<Author>Ursus62
<Content>Nice hotel in Union Square My wife and I concluded our honeymoon with 3 nights at the Sir Francis Drake.The keyword here is service. The staff, from the front desk to the doormen, goes all out for the guests. Requests for extra towels were promptly answered and room service was perfect.The location is on Powell Street, a block from Union Square, and on a main cable car line. If you don't like street noise, book a room on the upper levels. We were on 5, and could hear the cable cars and traffic -- not a problem for us, but could be for others. As with every other downtown SF hotel, be prepared to pay for cab rides that can get expensive ($20 to the hotel from the Legion of Honor/Lincoln Park area, and $10 to Fisherman's Wharf). However, it beats trying to drive and navigate this city.The upstairs bar, Harry Denton's, isn't much. They promote it heavily in the hotel as a cocktail/piano bar, but the night we were there, it was a DJ playing hip-hop remixes. Absolutely no different than any other club. Try The Top of the Mark instead if you want a low-key place for after hours drinks.It should be said this is an old-style hotel, meaning rooms are smaller than modern construction and bathrooms are as well. If you need spacious accomodations, go elsewhere. The room decor was a little dated. Water pressure was good though, to the point that toilets flushed overhead could be heard in our room. For us, a source of more amusement than concern. The rooms are said to be undergoing renovation, which may solve the decor issues, but not the size. We did not attempt internet connection, nor did we watch TV, so we can't comment on those features.Again, the high point was exceptional guest service. We are prepared to make this our home in SF.

<Author>Reeskers
<Content>There are MUCH better hotels in San Francisco My husband and I spent two nights at the Sir Francis Drake this past weekend, he was a groomsman in a wedding and the reception was being held at the hotel. I really did not want to stay at the hotel with the wedding party, having read the reviews on Trip Adviser and knowing that there are SO MANY better hotels around Union Square that we have stayed at before. We received a discounted room rate of $149 per night for a 'deluxe king' room, and paid an additional $45 per night for valet parking. I don't have a problem paying this kind of money for a hotel, as long as it is worth the price. I did NOT find this to be true for the Sir Francis Drake.Our 'deluxe king' room was nothing more than a basic hotel room with a king size bed. The room was about 200 square feet, we were in #712. In fact, it seemed smaller than usual because we had a bigger bed. The deco-style decor and furnishings, though not my taste, were colorful and tacky, but in good shape. As reported in an earlier review, it is true that the one small window was so dirty that you could barely see out of it. The real problem that I had was with the bathroom. It was so incredibly small that my husband and I could not be in there together. I guess that I would have been able to overlook the small size of the bathroom had it not been so disgusting.The bathtub had stains on the bottom and huge cracks all the way across the tile wall that were badly patched. There was mold and mildew on the ceiling and the surrounding walls. The ventilation duct was taped over so there was no air circulation in the bathroom, though keeping the bathroon door open and blasting the a/c helped a little. The shower curtain had mold on it as well. The faucet in the sink constantly dripped and the drain from the sink dripped on the floor (the housekeeping staff left a lovely washcloth there to absorb the water). The wood threshold leading into the bathroom was loose and half rotted (water damage?) and our toilet seat was barely attached to the toilet. It was the worst bathroom I have ever seen in a hotel. It was the consensus of others in the wedding party that there rooms were just as bad. Luckily we didn't have to spend much time in them. It was obvious that the bride and groom didn't check out the rooms before booking their reception at the hotel, there is no way that they would have chosen this place for their guests.I do have only good things to say about the catering/special event staff and the facilities for the wedding reception. The room was beautiful and the food was excellent. If you are visiting San Francisco, do some research and you will find a much better place to stay with just as good of a location. My husband says he will listen to me next time about where we stay. :)  
<Date>Aug 7, 2006

<Author>Academic_Excellence
<Content>Class and comfort--for our entire company! This summer I booked my NY company for a week-long leadership retreat at the Sir Francis Drake. Just before we left, I was notified of negative reviews on Trip Advisor.com, and it made me a little nervous. However, our entire stay was perfect--without one single complaint from our staff of 47 people (believe me, I would have heard about it!!) Instead, all I heard were raves from everyone. A few even extended their stay at the Drake for a personal vacation.The hotel is gorgeous, clean and classy, and ideally located near tons of shopping and restaurants of every kind. A cable car runs right in front of the hotel and takes you in 10 minutes to the Fisherman's Wharf, and Chinatown is within a two-minute walk. Best of all, the hotel staff--from the front desk to the caterers to the maintenance workers--were all professional, prompt and very friendly. Even the catered food (and we ordered the most inexpensive variety) was delicious.All in all, the hotel gave us class-A service for a great bargain price. I got big kudos from our company directors for booking us there, so--what more can I say?--THANK YOU Drake Hotel!!!

<Author>terriraven
<Content>ok, but won't be back We are a family of 4 and stayed on the 10th floor. Room was tiny, no fridge, and small bathroom. Room stuffy unless air conditioner constantly running. One window that one could see out of only if you stood on your tip-toes, but then you find out the view of the old buildings below are not worth it. Window did not open. However, room clean and well-painted; bathtub is very long and has a very large drain with lots of suction when draining-watch out! No vent in bathroom so could not leave door closed. We had to call everyday for extra bath towels because they would only supply 2. If you like a great view, good music/dancing and appetizers/drinks, highly recommend the Starlight room on the 21st floor; however, the hostess is a bit gruff, like a KGB agent. Had oysters and we crunched on shell particles that had not been cleaned properly when opened. Call ahead for a reservation. Also highly recommended is Scala restaurant downstairs. Again, make reservations days in advance. You can do this via e-mail. Lots of good eating places nearby, especially when you have children. Recommend Lori's Diner just across the street-great variety. Cable car stop is conveniently located and you can take it all the say down to the wharf area.

<Content>Not even if you paid me a million pound....I would never stay here again This hotel was my final destination on my round the world trip before jetting back to England. I had stayed in fantastic hotels in Singapore, Sydney and Tahiti and to stay here was such a disappointment that coming home and going back to work didn't seem to tedious! To be honest, it sounded liked rats or mice, put it this way, it wasn't human! They only smoking room left was a few floors down and I was warned that it was a little small. SMALL????!!!!! you couldn't swing a cat in it! The double bed took up the whole floor space and it was situated right by the lifts. Constant noise all day and night. The view out the window was of a brick wall, but I thought 'heck, you are only sleeping here, go explore San Francisco'.That was the plan until, on the 3rd morning at the hotel, the shower stopped working. After 5 phone calls to maintenance, and 3 hours later, someone came up to have a look at it and I was told there is a problem with the water affecting a few rooms on that floor. But I was assured that it would be fixed in good time. After a quick 'sink' wash, I headed out, only to return some hours later to find that the shower still didn't work. To cut a long story short, it took the hotel 48 hours to get it fixed. I was offered no real apology and had to ask to use another room to get a shower. Apparently, they were all booked up to move me on a permanent basis. Unbelieveable! Would I stay here again? Not even if you got me in a first class seat to San Francisco from Heathrow and gave me a million pounds to stay in this hotel. Do yourself a favour, book elsewhere.

<Author>firsttimeinvegas
<Content>Great location! We stayed at the Sir Francis Drake Feb. 15-20. The location was great! The rooms were small, but nice. Five of us were in town for a Coldwell Banker Conference. Three in our group shared a room. The room was a little small for three, so they asked for an upgrade. They got a larger room with a sofa bed and two bathrooms for $40 more per night! We took the cable car to Union Square  Fisherman's Wharf. Just hopped on it right out front! I highly recommend the Golddust around the corner. Great Bar, live music, good time. The Starlight room has an amazing view of the city. It was a very romantic place. We had a wonderful meal in China Town at The House of Nan King. The food is good  a fun atmosphere!We didn't get to go to Alcatraz because the tours were sold out. Make a reservation!I loved San Francisco, I will be back! I would stay at the Sir Francis Drake again. It isn't the Ritz, but I didn't pay for the Ritz!

<Author>gsaz
<Content>Superficially grand, but scratch the surface... .... and you find an old, poorly maintained place. My wife and I spent an evening at the SFD to catch a play down the street, just off Union Square. We'd had a nice post-theatre meal last year at the hotel restaurant, Scala's, and thought the hotel would be worth a try. The location is terrific - just off Union Square, on the cable car line, etc. We'd stayed at another Kimpton property in Boston and were impressed by the hip neo-classic styling in the rooms and the attitude of the place. Well, at the Drake, the look comes off like an old Hollywood starlet who's now getting by on cat food.  It has a beautiful old turn of the century lobby with some of Kimpton's signature touches - nouveau high-style furnishings, etc. - the stylistic elements of which repeat in the rooms, per Kimpton's formula. But it comes across as too formulaic here, and a band-aid on some real problems. Such as: paper-thin walls between the rooms; sooty windows; poor temperature control throughout the hotel (about 55潞 in the lobby on the chilly day, okay, but at their retro rooftop lounge, Harry Denton's Starlight Room it was also downright chilly - no budget for, say, a Home Depot thermostat?). Our bathroom had only a handicapped shower mounted at nose level - necessitating a crouch to get wet (we never requested this type of room, and the place was clearly not full). Above the shower stall, a hole in the wall covered by a rectangle of white plastic held in place by some old white fabric tape. (!) The hallways were renovated in a half-baked way: hip-ish light fixtures but depressing brown walls, beat up doors, and a vague rotting smell. We won't be returning soon - the Drake has potential to be a flashy retro hotel experience, but Kimpton needs to pump some serious dough into it to make it a liveable place again.  
<Date>Feb 19, 2006

<Content>We came away totally satisfyed Like others, we had some reservations about the mixed reviews about this hotel and didn't know what to expect; needless to say that the hotel completely exceeded our expectations. You can get a good deal from the discout internet sites like Hotwire. The service was courteous and professional, and unlike other hotels, which are cookie cutter copies of each other, Sir Francis Drake is distinctive and eclectic. Sure the hotel shows some of its age, especially in the bathrooms, but the first room we were in was well appointed and clean, with a large TV; although on the smaller side, anyone used to traveling in Europe and NYC will not feel uncomfortable. The air conditioner was in the window, but this was not obtrusive at all.We also dined at La Scala; great food and service and had a drink in the Starlight room, which offers one of the best views of the city in an exceedingly elegant setting. The service was superb; one evening we had some friends stay with us. We asked for a cot at 2am, but they gave a larger room with double beds at no extra cost.Finally, you can鈥檛 possibly beat this location; a block from Union Square and walking distance to Nob Hill and China town. Go ahead, try this place out!! You can probably get it between $70-90 a night on one of the discount websites.

<Author>imjimsharp
<Content>"I value my integrity" Was the mantra of the staff. When I asked for a nice room, the front desk clerk told us, I value my integrity, so I must tell you, this hotel is very old. I will do my best.We arrive in our room to find that it is a 9'x21' Box. The window was partially blocked by the window air conditioner, which was okay cause the window was SOOOO filthy that you couldn't really see outside. Fortunately, we brought our personal DVD player (the television selection was horrible. The TV was old with a bad picture. I plugged the DVD player into the tv's rca jacks, but the tv wouldn't accept the signal. When I called guest services the clerk told me, I value my integrity. Our televisions are very old. I don't think they accept a signal from a DVD player. Hmm, I am beggining to smell a theme. If a guest asks a question about the hotel, Just tell them that you value your integrity, but the hotel hasn't been renovated in 78 years. They will understand. If the guest doesn't seem appeased by your honesty, offer them an upgrade, for an additional fee. If you REALLY value your integrity, find another job. I am not taking potshots at the employees, but come on, you don't have to use a gun to steal from people..This hotel is a great example of owner milking the name of a (formerly) grand property for all it is worth. They charge a premium, and deliver NOTHING. Not a cup of coffee, not a newspaper, nothing, nada....squat.This is the second Kimpton property that we have stayed at that did not meet our expectations, the first was the Villa Florence. Same story, smaller scale. At least the Villa Florence had an afternoon wine reception so that you could get good and drunk and forget about how you were ripped off.IF YOU ARE LARGE (in the caboose) do not under any circumstances check into the hotel. The space between the sink and the bathroom wall in the toilet area is VERY tight. We are not overweight (by today's standards) and I knew that another 50 lbs. and I would have a problem. How embarassing would that phone call be when you can not get off the pot.If you are unfortunate enough to be reading this from the Sir Francis Drake (SFD), don't waste your money in their restaurants, go across the street and eat at Sears Fine Foods. This place is legendary, for a good reason. They have the best breakfasts I have eaten in my life. The corned beef hash is to die for. And the little swedish pancakes are irresistible. Since I am on the subject of food, check out Anjou, 44 Campton Place, just 1 1/2 block from the SFD. This little French restaurant is amazing. A real gem. My wife and I have eaten there several times and have never been disappointed. We have spent considerable time in Paris and this food rivals, if not exceeds what we found in France. Last night we had 2 large appetizers (the toasted brioche of duck foie gras, imported from France with heart leek salad and sauteed apples) and one special entree which is usually the wild salmon with mushroom and something mousse in a puff pastry. It was all absolutely fabulous and with a bottle of napa merlot, the bill came to $105.00!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Ideal location for cable cars Step out of the lobby and there's a cable car stop right outside. We loved this way of getting around and bought a 3 day MUNI pass for $18 which more than paid for itself. The hotel was ideally situated for getting to all the main attractions easily and we'd definitely stay in the Downtown area again as a base for sightseeing. Our room was small, but fine for a city hotel and we decided not to ask to move. The guidebooks were spot on with the description of the hotel: faded grandeur and the old chipped bathroom tile, but comfy beds, no skimping on decent toiletries and overall we were very happy. The staff were all very helpful and professional, and the concierges were brilliant at suggesting and booking restaurants. Top tip: All the guidebooks recommend breakfast at Sears Fine Foods directly opposite the hotel (queues every day) but we ate there one day and every other day went back for the breakfast in the hotel restaurant - Scalas. Food and service was excellent and the bill was not that different.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not worth your time and money I travel to San Francisco often but usually stay at the Westin St. Francis or the Clift. My wife arrange this stay based on a conference she was attending. I was disappointed by the hotel and do not believe that the relatively cheaper rates (compared to other hotels in the downtown area) make it worth it to stay here. The main basis for the disappointment was the room itself, which I found small and unattractive. Placing the veneer of vintage boutique did not make it any more appealing. The closets were too shallow to put coats in. The bathroom was particularly difficult to manuever in from a space perspective. The embedded hair dryer in the bathroom had a large piece of casing missing and smoked when turned on! While we were given a replacement, amazingly the original smoking dryer was never replaced. I would put even odds on the possibility that it will not be replaced for a while. The placement of electrical outlets near the desk was very inconvenient, forcing me to work sitting on the bed. Finally, the room service was temporarily unavailable two out of three nights, which was frustrating.I will say that the wireless access was seamless, but I think that this should be expected of most hotels in SF.

<Content>Spend Your Money Elsewhere Yes, the lobby is lovely. The staff is relatively polite and accomodating. The carpets are in bad need of replacement, (most hotels know that carpets should be replaced at least every two years, depending on traffic). The decor itself is outdated, which would be fine if we were not paying a high price. It felt like we were sleeping in a 1994 children's movie. We had a large picture window with a fantastic view of... the roof. Oh, and the dozens of beer bottles left by past victims who obviously tool advantage of oppurtunity.The bathroom was clean and cute, (ugh, but for the badly needed to be replaced wallpaper). I live in a house built in 1905, so I am used to antique fixtures. Yes, the Aveda products are nice. The hotel sent me an online survey and I was frank in my response. Customer service was kind enough to reply, and informed me that the building is scheduled for renovation in 2006. She mentioned that the hotel is old and the srestle wih difficulties regarding age, but I stay in old hotels all the time and have never experienced issues like this. This is in fact one of my worst stays in a hotel ever.Perhaps next year things shall improve, but I will never really know.
